## Chapter: American Foreign Policy: A Comprehensive Analysis

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will be examining the relationship between the United States and Argentina in terms of foreign policy. The United States has a long history of involvement in Argentina, dating back to the early 19th century when the U.S. supported Argentina's independence from Spain. Since then, the two countries have had a complex and often tumultuous relationship, with periods of cooperation and conflict.

Throughout this chapter, we will explore the various aspects of U.S. foreign policy towards Argentina, including economic, political, and military relations. We will also examine the impact of U.S. involvement in Argentina on both countries and the region as a whole. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of the dynamics of the U.S.-Argentina relationship and its significance in the global arena.




### Introduction

The United States has a long and complex history of involvement in Nigeria, one of the largest and most populous countries in Africa. This chapter will provide a comprehensive analysis of the U.S. foreign policy towards Nigeria, examining the historical context, key events, and current dynamics of this relationship.

The United States has been involved in Nigeria since the 19th century, primarily through missionary work and trade. However, it was not until the mid-20th century that the U.S. began to actively engage in foreign policy towards Nigeria. This chapter will delve into the reasons behind this shift, including the U.S.'s growing economic interests in Nigeria and its desire to contain the spread of communism in Africa.

The chapter will also explore the key events that have shaped the U.S.-Nigeria relationship, such as the Nigerian Civil War and the rise of oil production in Nigeria. These events have had a profound impact on the U.S.'s approach to Nigeria, and this chapter will examine how the U.S. has responded to these developments.

Finally, this chapter will discuss the current state of U.S. foreign policy towards Nigeria, including the U.S.'s role in addressing Nigeria's political, economic, and social challenges. It will also examine the future prospects for this relationship, considering the potential for further cooperation and conflict between the two nations.

Through this comprehensive analysis, readers will gain a deeper understanding of the complex dynamics of the U.S.-Nigeria relationship and the role that U.S. foreign policy has played in shaping this relationship. 




### Subsection: 20.1 U.S.-Nigeria Security Cooperation

The United States and Nigeria have a complex relationship when it comes to security cooperation. This relationship has been shaped by various factors, including the Chibok schoolgirls kidnapping, the Africa Crisis Response Initiative, and the Global Coalition to Defeat ISIS (D-ISIS).

#### Chibok Schoolgirls Kidnapping

The Chibok schoolgirls kidnapping in April 2014 brought international attention to the security issues in Nigeria. In response to this incident, the United States committed to providing assistance to Nigeria. This assistance included sending an interdisciplinary team to assist the Nigerian military, initially comprising 38 members, including two Federal Bureau of Investigation hostage specialists and several military intelligence analysts. 

However, the U.S. team faced challenges in their efforts to assist Nigeria. The Nigerian government was slow to accept and implement the U.S.'s offer of assistance, leading to tensions between the U.S. team and Nigerian officials. This early stage of the mission also saw disagreements over the use of U.S. resources, with Nigerian officials reportedly questioning the need for certain resources, such as manned intelligence, surveillance, and reconnaissance flights.

#### Africa Crisis Response Initiative

The Africa Crisis Response Initiative (ACRI) has been a key platform for U.S.-Nigeria security cooperation. Established in 2007, ACRI has been a hub for cooperation against piracy, drug trafficking, oil theft, and border fraud in the Gulf of Guinea. Nigeria's membership of ACRI has allowed for increased U.S. military support, including through the Africa Military Education Program and the Trans-Sahara Counterterrorism Partnership.

#### Global Coalition to Defeat ISIS (D-ISIS)

Nigeria is a member of the Global Coalition to Defeat ISIS (D-ISIS), and the U.S. and Nigeria co-hosted a virtual D-ISIS conference in October 2020. This membership has further strengthened the security cooperation between the U.S. and Nigeria, with both countries working together to combat ISIS and other terrorist threats.

#### U.S. Military Support

The U.S. has provided significant military support to Nigeria, including through the Africa Partnership Station and the Global Coalition to Defeat ISIS (D-ISIS). In addition, a member of the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers has been stationed permanently at the Kainji Airbase in Nigeria, to oversee key U.S. Africa Command projects there.

In conclusion, the U.S.-Nigeria security cooperation has been shaped by various factors, including the Chibok schoolgirls kidnapping, the Africa Crisis Response Initiative, and the Global Coalition to Defeat ISIS (D-ISIS). While there have been challenges, the cooperation between the two countries has been crucial in addressing the security issues in Nigeria.




### Subsection: 20.2 U.S.-Nigeria Trade Relations

The United States and Nigeria have a complex relationship when it comes to trade. This relationship has been shaped by various factors, including the Nigeria-United States Bi-National Commission, the Trade and Investment Framework Agreement, and the Africa Growth and Opportunity Act.

#### Nigeria-United States Bi-National Commission

The Nigeria-United States Bi-National Commission (BNC) is a platform for dialogue and cooperation between the two nations. It was established in 1999 and has been instrumental in facilitating trade and investment between the two countries. The BNC has been particularly important in addressing trade issues and promoting economic growth.

#### Trade and Investment Framework Agreement

In 2000, Nigeria and the United States signed a Trade and Investment Framework Agreement. This agreement provides a framework for trade and investment between the two countries and includes provisions for market access, intellectual property rights, and investment protection. The agreement also includes a mechanism for resolving trade disputes.

#### Africa Growth and Opportunity Act

The Africa Growth and Opportunity Act (AGOA) was passed by the United States Congress in 2000. It provides eligible African countries, including Nigeria, with preferential access to the U.S. market for certain products. This has been particularly beneficial for Nigeria, given its sizeable market and its status as the third largest market for U.S. exports in Sub-Saharan Africa.

#### Trade Imbalance

Despite the efforts to increase U.S. exports to Nigeria, there has been a persistent trade imbalance between the two countries. In 2019, Nigeria was the United States' second largest export destination in Sub-Saharan Africa, with a trade deficit of $1.4 billion. This deficit has been largely due to Nigeria's dominance in fuel exports to the United States.

#### U.S.-Nigeria Trade Relations: A Case Study

The relationship between the United States and Nigeria provides a case study of the complexities and challenges of trade relations between developed and developing countries. While the United States has been a major trading partner for Nigeria, the trade imbalance and the challenges of increasing U.S. exports to Nigeria highlight the need for a more balanced and mutually beneficial trade relationship.




### Subsection: 20.3a U.S. Criticism of Nigeria's Human Rights Record

The United States has been a vocal critic of Nigeria's human rights record, particularly in regards to police brutality and extrajudicial killings. This criticism has been a significant factor in the U.S.-Nigeria human rights dialogue.

#### Police Brutality and Extrajudicial Killings

The United States has consistently raised concerns about police brutality and extrajudicial killings in Nigeria. The U.S. Department of State's 2020 Country Reports on Human Rights Practices noted that security forces, including the police and military, committed numerous human rights abuses, including unlawful killings, arbitrary detention, and torture. The report also highlighted the lack of accountability for these abuses, which it said was a major human rights issue in the country.

The U.S. government has also expressed concern about the use of excessive force by Nigerian security forces, particularly the Special Anti-Robbery Squad (SARS). The U.S. Embassy in Nigeria has repeatedly called on the Nigerian government to investigate and prosecute security personnel who commit human rights abuses.

#### U.S.-Nigeria Human Rights Dialogue

The U.S.-Nigeria human rights dialogue has been a key forum for discussing these issues. The dialogue, which is held annually, provides an opportunity for the U.S. government to raise its concerns about Nigeria's human rights record and to press for improvements.

The dialogue has been particularly focused on police brutality and extrajudicial killings. In recent years, the U.S. government has urged the Nigerian government to implement reforms to address these issues, including by establishing an independent body to investigate security force abuses and by providing training for security personnel on human rights and international law.

#### U.S. Criticism and Nigeria's Response

Nigeria has been responsive to U.S. criticism of its human rights record. In response to U.S. concerns about police brutality and extrajudicial killings, the Nigerian government has taken steps to address these issues.

In 2020, the Nigerian government disbanded the Special Anti-Robbery Squad (SARS) in response to widespread protests over police brutality. The government also established a new police unit, the Special Weapons and Tactics (SWAT) team, to address issues of police misconduct.

The Nigerian government has also taken steps to improve accountability for human rights abuses. In 2019, it established the Presidential Panel on the Reform of the Special Anti-Robbery Squad (SARS), which is tasked with investigating and prosecuting security personnel who commit human rights abuses.

Despite these efforts, the U.S. government continues to express concern about Nigeria's human rights record. It has called on the Nigerian government to continue to address these issues and to ensure that all Nigerians are treated with dignity and respect.




### Subsection: 20.3b U.S. Aid to Nigeria for Human Rights Training

The United States has been a major provider of aid to Nigeria, with a significant portion of this aid being directed towards human rights training. This aid is part of the U.S. government's broader strategy to promote democracy and human rights in Nigeria.

#### U.S. Aid for Human Rights Training

The United States has provided significant aid to Nigeria for human rights training, particularly for security personnel. This aid is aimed at improving the human rights performance of Nigerian security forces, including the police and the military.

One of the key programs for this aid is the African Contingency Operations Training and Assistance (ACOTA) program. This program, which is managed by the U.S. Department of Defense, provides training and assistance to African countries, including Nigeria, in areas such as peacekeeping, stability operations, and human rights.

The ACOTA program has been particularly focused on training Nigerian security personnel in human rights. This training includes instruction on international human rights law, as well as practical training on how to respect and protect human rights in the course of their duties.

#### Impact of U.S. Aid on Human Rights in Nigeria

The U.S. aid for human rights training has had a significant impact on human rights in Nigeria. The training has helped to improve the human rights performance of Nigerian security forces, particularly the police and the military.

For example, the U.S. aid has helped to reduce the number of unlawful killings by Nigerian security forces. According to the U.S. Department of State's 2020 Country Reports on Human Rights Practices, the number of unlawful killings by security forces has decreased significantly in recent years. This is largely due to the training provided by the U.S. aid.

The U.S. aid has also helped to improve the accountability of Nigerian security forces for human rights abuses. The training has equipped security personnel with the knowledge and skills to investigate and prosecute human rights abuses, thereby contributing to the rule of law in Nigeria.

#### Challenges and Future Directions

Despite the significant impact of the U.S. aid, there are still challenges to be addressed. One of the main challenges is the lack of institutionalization of human rights training in Nigeria. This means that the improvements achieved through the U.S. aid are not sustained after the training ends.

To address this challenge, the U.S. aid should be accompanied by efforts to institutionalize human rights training in Nigeria. This could include the establishment of a human rights training center, the integration of human rights training into the curriculum of security force training institutions, and the development of a system for monitoring and evaluating the human rights performance of Nigerian security forces.

In addition, the U.S. aid should be complemented by efforts to address the root causes of human rights abuses in Nigeria. This could include addressing the lack of resources and equipment for Nigerian security forces, as well as addressing the political and social factors that contribute to human rights abuses.




### Subsection: 20.3c U.S.-Nigeria Dialogue on Religious Freedom

The United States and Nigeria have a complex relationship when it comes to religious freedom. While the United States has been a vocal critic of Nigeria's human rights record, particularly in regards to religious freedom, it has also been a major trading partner and ally. This has led to a delicate balance in their relationship, with the United States often using its economic leverage to push for improvements in human rights while also maintaining strong diplomatic ties.

#### U.S.-Nigeria Dialogue on Religious Freedom

The United States and Nigeria have engaged in a long-standing dialogue on religious freedom. This dialogue has been driven by the United States' concerns over the treatment of religious minorities in Nigeria, particularly Christians and Muslims. The United States has consistently raised these concerns at the highest levels of the Nigerian government, including during high-level visits and in bilateral discussions.

One of the key issues in this dialogue has been the establishment of sharia-based penal codes in 12 states in Nigeria. These codes, which are used in addition to the country's secular legal system, have been a source of concern for the United States due to their potential to discriminate against religious minorities. The United States has consistently urged Nigeria to ensure that these codes are applied in a manner that respects the rights of all Nigerians, regardless of their religious beliefs.

#### U.S. Concerns over Religious Freedom in Nigeria

The United States has been particularly concerned about the treatment of religious minorities in Nigeria. This includes the targeting of Christians by Islamic extremist groups, such as Boko Haram, as well as the discrimination faced by Christians in the predominantly Muslim north of the country. The United States has also raised concerns about the treatment of Muslims in the predominantly Christian south, particularly in regards to the establishment of private schools by religious associations.

The United States has also been critical of the Nigerian government's response to these issues. While the government has taken some steps to address these concerns, such as the creation of the Islamic Forum, the United States has argued that these efforts have been insufficient and that more needs to be done to protect the rights of all Nigerians, regardless of their religious beliefs.

#### U.S. Aid for Religious Freedom Training

In addition to its dialogue on religious freedom, the United States has also provided aid to Nigeria for training on religious freedom. This aid has been aimed at improving the understanding and respect for religious freedom among Nigerian security forces and government officials.

One of the key programs for this aid is the International Religious Freedom (IRF) program, which is managed by the U.S. Department of State. This program provides training and assistance to Nigerian security forces and government officials on international religious freedom standards and best practices. It also supports civil society organizations that promote religious freedom in Nigeria.

The IRF program has been particularly focused on improving the treatment of religious minorities in Nigeria. This includes training security forces on how to respect the rights of religious minorities, as well as promoting dialogue and understanding between different religious communities.

#### Impact of U.S. Aid on Religious Freedom in Nigeria

The U.S. aid for religious freedom training has had a significant impact on religious freedom in Nigeria. The training has helped to improve the understanding and respect for religious freedom among Nigerian security forces and government officials. It has also helped to promote dialogue and understanding between different religious communities, leading to a more inclusive and tolerant society.

However, there is still much work to be done. The United States will continue to push for improvements in religious freedom in Nigeria, and will use its economic leverage and diplomatic ties to advocate for the rights of all Nigerians, regardless of their religious beliefs.

### Conclusion

The relationship between the United States and Nigeria in terms of foreign policy has been a complex one, with both countries facing their own unique challenges and opportunities. The United States has been a major player in Nigeria's political and economic landscape, providing aid and support in various forms. However, this relationship has not been without its controversies, particularly in regards to human rights and religious freedom.

The United States has been a vocal critic of Nigeria's human rights record, particularly in regards to the treatment of religious minorities. This has led to a delicate balance in their relationship, with the United States often using its economic leverage to push for improvements in human rights while also maintaining strong diplomatic ties.

Despite these challenges, the United States and Nigeria have been able to work together on various issues, such as counterterrorism efforts and economic development. This has led to a strong partnership between the two countries, with both nations recognizing the importance of maintaining a positive relationship for their own national interests.

## Chapter: Chapter 21: U.S. Foreign Policy and South Africa

### Introduction

The relationship between the United States and South Africa has been a complex and evolving one, shaped by a multitude of factors including political ideology, economic interests, and global power dynamics. This chapter will delve into the intricacies of this relationship, examining the historical context, key events, and current state of affairs between these two nations.

The United States has long been a major player in global affairs, and its foreign policy decisions have had a profound impact on countries around the world. South Africa, with its unique history and political landscape, has been no exception. The chapter will explore how the United States' foreign policy has been shaped by its perception of South Africa, and how this perception has evolved over time.

The chapter will also examine the various factors that have influenced the United States' approach to South Africa, including the country's apartheid regime, its transition to democracy, and its current political and economic landscape. It will also delve into the role of the United States in South Africa's history, from its support for the apartheid regime to its role in the country's transition to democracy.

Finally, the chapter will discuss the current state of the relationship between the United States and South Africa, examining areas of cooperation and conflict, and exploring potential future developments in this important global partnership. 

Through this comprehensive analysis, readers will gain a deeper understanding of the complex dynamics of U.S. foreign policy and its impact on South Africa.
